### 点(點)茶 → 点(點) → 占 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 点(點)茶 → 茶
- **definition:** tea
- **pinyin:** chá
- **components:**
  - 艹
    - cǎo
    - grass
  - 余
    - yú
    - I; surplus
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 艹 (cǎo, "grass") + phonetic 余 (yú) ->
    - modified from archaic 荼 (bitter plant) for tea
  - **interpretation:** The character 茶 (chá, "tea") combines 艹 (cǎo, "grass") as the semantic element, indicating a plant-related concept, with 余 (yú) serving as the phonetic component. Originally, 茶 was a modification of the archaic character 荼 which referred to a 'bitter plant.' This association with a bitter plant reflects the historical use of tea leaves, which have a bitter taste, thereby making 茶 appropriate for representing 'tea.'
- **examples:**
  - 奶奶每天早上喝茶。
    - Nǎinai měitiān zǎoshang hē chá.
    - Grandma drinks tea every morning.
  - 这(這)家茶馆(館)的绿(綠)茶味道很好。
    - Zhè jiā cháguǎn de lǜchá wèidào hěn hǎo.
    - The green tea at this teahouse tastes very good.
  - 你想喝红(紅)茶还(還)是绿(綠)茶？
    - Nǐ xiǎng hē hóngchá háishì lǜchá?
    - Do you want to drink black tea or green tea?
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 艹
- **definition:** grass
- **pinyin:** cǎo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts blades of grass
  - **interpretation:** 艹 is a pictogram representing grass or plants, resembling blades of grass. It is commonly used as a radical in other characters related to grass or vegetation.
- **examples:**
  - 他写(寫)字时(時)用艹作草字的偏旁。
    - Tā xiězì shí yòng cǎo zuò cǎozì de piānpáng.
    - He uses '艹' as the radical for grass in his characters.
  - 春天到来(來)时(時)，艹生长(長)得很快。
    - Chūntiān dàolái shí, cǎo shēngzhǎng de hěn kuài.
    - When spring arrives, grass grows rapidly.
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘)
- **traditional:** 餘
- **definition:** I; surplus
- **pinyin:** yú
- **components:**
  - 食
    - shí
    - food
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 食 (shí, 'food') + phonetic 余(餘) (yú, 'I') ->
    - remains of food ->
    - 'excess, surplus'
  - **interpretation:** The character 餘 evolved to represent the concept of 'excess' or 'surplus' through a phono-semantic compound. It combines the semantic component 食 (shí, 'food'), representing food or consumption, with the phonetic component 余(餘) (yú, 'I'), to indicate leftovers or remains of food. This directly suggests an aspect of having more than what is needed, thus an 'excess' or 'surplus'.
  - **simplification:** The traditional character 餘 was simplified to 余 by removing the semantic component 食 (shí, 'food'), leaving only the phonetic component.
- **examples:**
  - 余(餘)愿(願)以诗(詩)书(書)为(為)乐(樂)。
    - Yú yuàn yǐ shīshū wéi lè.
    - I wish to take pleasure in poetry and books.
  - 余(餘)在此地，心安吾归(歸)。
    - Yú zài cǐdì, xīn ān wú guī.
    - I am here, at peace and at home.
  - 余(餘)莫负(負)此生。
    - Yú mò fù cǐ shēng.
    - I should not waste this life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 余](@media/glyph4f59.png)
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食
- **definition:** food
- **pinyin:** shí
- **components:**
  - 亼
    - jí
    - assemble
  - 𠊊
    - jí
    - bowl with stand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** Pictogram
  - **description:** 亼 (jí, "assemble") over a pictographic bowl of rice on a stand, symbolized by 𠊊 (jí, "bowl with stand")
  - **interpretation:** Initially, the character 食 (shí, "eat") visually represented a mouth over a bowl of rice, conveying the act of eating or a meal intuitively through this imagery.
- **examples:**
  - 他食得很快。
    - Tā shí dé hěn kuài.
    - He eats very quickly.
  - 我准(準)备(備)午食，与(與)朋友共享佳肴(餚)。
    - Wǒ zhǔnbèi wǔ shí, yǔ péngyǒu gòngxiǎng jiāyáo.
    - I am preparing lunch to share a delicious meal with my friends.
  - 民以食为(為)天。
    - Mín yǐ shí wéi tiān.
    - Food is regarded as the most important element for the people.
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食 → 亼
- **definition:** assemble
- **pinyin:** jí
- **components:**
  - 入
    - rù
    - enter
  - 一
    - yī
    - one
  - 今
    - jīn
    - now
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 入 (rù, "enter") + 一 (yī, "one") =
    - gathering from three sides ->
    - original form of 今 (jīn, "now")
  - **interpretation:** 亼 (jī, "open mouth flipped upside down") originally represented the action of gathering, with 入 (rù, "enter") suggesting bringing things together and 一 (yī, "one") implying unification into a single entity. This concept aligns traditionally with 集 (jí, "gather"), where the sense of gathering from three sides connects to assembling or coming together. The visual comparison to an open mouth reversed is a less common interpretation, relating to a shape rather than function.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 亼](@media/glyph4ebc.png)
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食 → 亼 → 入
- **definition:** enter
- **pinyin:** rù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** An arrowhead indicating 'to enter'
  - **interpretation:** The character 入(rù, 'enter') visually represents the concept of entering, with the form resembling an arrowhead suggesting movement through an opening.
- **examples:**
  - 请(請)入座。
    - Qǐng rùzuò.
    - Please take a seat.
  - 学(學)生走入校园(園)，开(開)始新学(學)期。
    - Xuéshēng zǒu rù xiàoyuán, kāishǐ xīn xuéqī.
    - The students enter the campus and start a new semester.
  - 游(遊)客走入古城，探索历(歷)史。
    - Yóukè zǒu rù gǔchéng, tànsuǒ lìshǐ.
    - The tourists enter the ancient city and explore its history.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 入](@media/glyph5165.png)
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食 → 亼 → 一
- **definition:** one
- **pinyin:** yī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** A horizontal stroke representing the concept of 'one'.
  - **interpretation:** The character 一(yī, "one") is a simple horizontal line signifying the singular and unified concept of 'one'. It directly represents being singular or the number one.
- **examples:**
  - 我有一个(個)苹(蘋)果。
    - Wǒ yǒu yī gè píngguǒ.
    - I have one apple.
  - 他只看到一只(隻)鸟(鳥)，飞(飛)进(進)了花园(園)。
    - Tā zhǐ kàn dào yī zhī niǎo, fēi jìn le huā yuán.
    - He only saw one bird, which flew into the garden.
  - 一条(條)直路通向远(遠)方。
    - Yī tiáo zhí lù tōng xiàng yuǎn fāng.
    - One straight road leads to the distance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 一](@media/glyph4e00.png)
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食 → 亼 → 今
- **definition:** now
- **pinyin:** jīn
- **components:**
  - 曰
    - yuē
    - to speak
  - 亼
    - jí
    - collect; assemble
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - 曰 (yuē, "to speak") inverted with 亼-like structure + horizontal stroke ->
    - original form implying 'not to speak' or 'keep in mouth'
  - **interpretation:** The character depicts an inverted version of 曰 (yuē, "to speak"), with a structure resembling 亼 and a horizontal stroke, representing something placed in the mouth, leading to the sense of 'keeping in the mouth' or 'not speaking'. This image of being contained or holding leads to 'now', as in holding or having the present moment.
- **examples:**
  - 今天的天气(氣)不错(錯)。
    - Jīntiān de tiānqì bùcuò.
    - Today's weather is nice.
  - 现(現)在是吃晚饭(飯)的时(時)候。
    - Xiànzài shì chī wǎnfàn de shíhòu.
    - Now is the time to have dinner.
  - 她今天特别(別)忙，没(沒)时(時)间(間)见(見)面。
    - Tā jīntiān tèbié máng, méi shíjiān jiànmiàn.
    - She is especially busy today and doesn't have time to meet.
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食 → 𠊊
- **definition:** bowl with stand
- **pinyin:** jí
- **components:**
  - 亼
    - jí
    - mouth
  - 皀
    - jí
    - bowl of rice on a stand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 亼 (mouth) over 皀 (bowl of rice on a stand) ->
    - depicts a bowl with a stand
  - **interpretation:** The character 𠊊 visually represents a mouth above a bowl of rice on a stand, indicating a utensil or vessel used for holding food. This image directly links to the idea of a 'bowl with stand.' The component 皀 specifically conveys the idea of a container or bowl elevated, which situates its primary meaning in the context of serving or holding food.
### 点(點)茶 → 茶 → 余(餘) → 食 → 𠊊 → 皀
- **definition:** bowl of rice on a stand
- **pinyin:** jí
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a bowl of rice on a stand ->
    - part of the radical 食 (shí, "food")
  - **interpretation:** The character 皀(bá, "acorn") depicts a bowl of rice on a stand, aligning it with food-related imagery.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 皀](@media/glyph7680.png)

## traditional tea whisking method

## 串串香
---
## skewered hot pot
### chuàn chuàn xiāng
---
- **definition:** skewered hot pot
- **pinyin:** chuàn chuàn xiāng
- **components:**
  - 串串
    - chuànchuàn
    - a series of skewers
  - 香
    - xiāng
    - fragrant; aromatic; savory
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** In this word, 串 (chuàn, "skewer") is the main concept of skewering food; repeated to 串串 (chuànchuàn, "a series of skewers"), and 香 (xiāng, "fragrant") refers to the aroma from cooking or seasoning, describing the aromatic quality of the dish.
  - **interpretation:** 串串 (chuànchuàn, "a series of skewers") signifies multiple skewered items, a defining characteristic of this dining style where small portions are cooked on skewers. 香 (xiāng, "fragrant") emphasizes the appealing scent released as the ingredients cook in the hot pot broth, drawing people in with its aroma. This describes a type of hot pot where individual skewers of ingredients are cooked in a communal pot, appealing both visually and aromatically.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)昨天晚上去吃了串串香。
    - Wǒmen zuótiān wǎnshàng qù chī le chuàn chuàn xiāng.
    - We went to eat skewered hot pot last night.
  - 小李特别(別)喜欢(歡)成都的串串香。
    - Xiǎo Lǐ tèbié xǐhuān Chéngdū de chuàn chuàn xiāng.
    - Xiao Li especially likes Chengdu's skewered hot pot.
  - 串串香的汤(湯)底有很多种(種)口味，可以根据(據)自己的喜好选(選)择(擇)。
    - Chuàn chuàn xiāng de tāngdǐ yǒu hěn duō zhǒng kǒuwèi, kěyǐ gēnjù zìjǐ de xǐhào xuǎnzé.
    - The skewered hot pot has many flavors of broth to choose from according to your preference.
### 串串香 → 串串
- **definition:** a series of skewers
- **pinyin:** chuànchuàn
- **components:**
  - 串
    - chuàn
    - string together; skewer
  - 串
    - chuàn
    - string together; skewer
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 串 (chuàn, "string together") + 串 (chuàn, "string together") refers to food items pierced and cooked on skewers.
  - **interpretation:** The repetition of 串 (chuàn, "string together") emphasizes the act of threading ingredients onto a skewer, which is common in street food culture where various meats and vegetables are skewered together and grilled.
- **examples:**
  - 我喜欢(歡)吃串串。
    - Wǒ xǐhuān chī chuànchuàn.
    - I like eating skewered food.
  - 冬天寒冷时(時)，串串让(讓)人感觉(覺)温(溫)暖。
    - Dōngtiān hánlěng shí, chuànchuàn ràng rén gǎnjué wēnnuǎn.
    - When winter is cold, skewers make people feel warm.
  - 夜市里(裡)，各种(種)美味的串串吸引顾(顧)客。
    - Yèshì lǐ, gèzhǒng měiwèi de chuànchuàn xīyǐn gùkè.
    - In the night market, various delicious skewers attract customers.
### 串串香 → 串串 → 串
- **definition:** string together; skewer
- **pinyin:** chuàn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts objects strung together
  - **interpretation:** The character 串(chuàn) visually represents the concept of objects strung together, often like beads or skewers. This straightforward pictographic representation effectively conveys its meaning as 'to string together' or 'skewer'.
- **examples:**
  - 他用铁(鐵)签(簽)串起葡萄，准(準)备(備)烧(燒)烤。
    - Tā yòng tiě qiān chuàn qǐ pútao, zhǔnbèi shāokǎo.
    - He skewered the grapes with an iron skewer, preparing for a barbecue.
  - 她把各色小灯(燈)笼(籠)串成一条(條)彩带(帶)，装(裝)点(點)夜宵。
    - Tā bǎ gèsè xiǎo dēnglóng chuàn chéng yī tiáo cǎidài, zhuāngdiǎn yèxiāo.
    - She strung various small lanterns together into a colorful ribbon, decorating the night market.
  - 老板让(讓)工人把散乱(亂)的零件串起来(來)，以便机(機)器组(組)装(裝)。
    - Lǎobǎn ràng gōngrén bǎ sǎnluàn de língjiàn chuàn qǐlái, yǐbiàn jīqì zǔzhuāng.
    - The boss had the workers string together the scattered parts, so that the machine could be assembled.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 串](@media/glyph4e32.png)
### 串串香 → 香
- **definition:** fragrant; aromatic; savory
- **pinyin:** xiāng
- **components:**
  - 黍
    - shǔ
    - glutinous millet
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
  - 甘
    - gān
    - sweet
  - 禾
    - hé
    - grain
  - 曰
    - yuē
    - say
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 黍 (shǔ, "glutinous millet") + 口 (kǒu, "mouth") ->
    - millet used for liquor ->
    - 甘 (gān, "sweet") replaced 口, indicating sweetness ->
    - 禾 + 曰 final form
  - **interpretation:** The character 香(xiāng) originated from showcasing millet as a beverage ingredient, hinting at the fragrant nature of such products. Over time, the components evolved to stress the sweet and fragrant aspect, becoming 禾 and 曰 to convey aroma.
- **examples:**
  - 花儿(兒)散发(發)出香气(氣)。
    - Huār sànfā chū xiāngqì.
    - The flowers emit a fragrant scent.
  - 这(這)汤(湯)闻(聞)起来(來)很香。
    - Zhè tāng wén qǐlái hěn xiāng.
    - This soup smells very fragrant.
  - 她的香水味迷人，让(讓)人陶醉。
    - Tā de xiāngshuǐ wèi mírén, ràng rén táozuì.
    - Her perfume is enchanting, making people intoxicated.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 香](@media/glyph9999.png)
### 串串香 → 香 → 黍
- **definition:** glutinous millet
- **pinyin:** shǔ
- **components:**
  - 禾
    - hé
    - cereal
  - 水
    - shuǐ
    - water
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts 禾 (hé, "cereal") with 水 (shuǐ, "water") under it ->
    - symbolizing millet with wine or its sticky nature
  - **interpretation:** The character 黍 (shǔ, "glutinous millet") visually combines the image of a cereal plant with droplets or signs of water beneath it, likely indicating the wine made from millet or its water-resistant qualities. Alternatively, it highlights millet's unique growing conditions.
- **examples:**
  - 秋天时(時)，农(農)夫收获(穫)黍。
    - Qiūtiān shí, nóngfū shōuhuò shǔ.
    - In autumn, the farmer harvests glutinous millet.
  - 古人以黍，寓意丰(豐)收。
    - Gǔrén yǐ shǔ, yùyì fēngshōu.
    - The ancients used glutinous millet to symbolize a bountiful harvest.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 黍](@media/glyph9ecd.png)
### 串串香 → 香 → 黍 → 禾
- **definition:** cereal
- **pinyin:** hé
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a stalk of grain or cereal plant
  - **interpretation:** The character 禾 (hé, 'grain') visually represents a plant with roots and leaves, focusing on the appearance of staple crops like rice or millet. This clearly conveys its meaning as it resembles the actual shape of a plant grown for its grain.
- **examples:**
  - 收获(穫)的禾香弥(彌)漫在田野中。
    - Shōuhuò de hé xiāng mímàn zài tiányě zhōng.
    - The fragrance of grain filled the fields.
  - 农(農)民辛勤耕作，收割禾穗。
    - Nóngmín xīnqín gēngzuò, shōugē hé suì.
    - The hardworking farmers harvested the ears of grain.
  - 春雨滋润(潤)了禾苗，预(預)示着(著)丰(豐)收。
    - Chūnyǔ zīrùn le hé miáo, yùshì zhe fēngshōu.
    - The spring rain nourished the grain seedlings, foreshadowing a bountiful harvest.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 禾](@media/glyph79be.png)
### 串串香 → 香 → 黍 → 水
- **definition:** water
- **pinyin:** shuǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts flowing water
  - **interpretation:** 水 (shuǐ, 'water') is a pictogram that directly represents the appearance of flowing water, making it intuitive and easy to recognize. Its simplicity and direct visual reference to its meaning have allowed it to remain unchanged over millennia.
- **examples:**
  - 水是一种(種)生命之源。
    - Shuǐ shì yī zhǒng shēngmìng zhī yuán.
    - Water is the source of life.
  - 夏天很热(熱)，喝水能解暑。
    - Xiàtiān hěn rè, hē shuǐ néng jiě shǔ.
    - It is very hot in summer, drinking water can relieve the heat.
  - 河水潺潺，沿岸绿(綠)树(樹)成荫(蔭)。
    - Hé shuǐ chánchán, yán'àn lǜshù chéng yīn.
    - The river flows babbling, and green trees along the bank provide shade.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 水](@media/glyph6c34.png)
### 串串香 → 香 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 串串香 → 香 → 甘
- **definition:** sweet
- **pinyin:** gān
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - 𠁿 ->
    - something sweet in an open mouth ->
    - 甘
  - **interpretation:** 甘 (gān, "sweet") is an ideogram depicting something sweet inside an open mouth. This visualization of taste illustrates the core concept of sweetness as directly related to the act of consuming something pleasant. This visual representation connects the sensory experience of sweetness with its meaning in the character.
- **examples:**
  - 蜂蜜很甘。
    - Fēngmì hěn gān.
    - Honey is very sweet.
  - 他的话(話)如甘露滋润(潤)了我的心。
    - Tā de huà rú gānlù zīrùnle wǒ de xīn.
    - His words nourished my heart like sweet dew.
  - 这(這)种(種)水果味道甘美。
    - Zhè zhǒng shuǐguǒ wèidào gān měi.
    - The taste of this fruit is sweet and delicious.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 甘](@media/glyph7518.png)
### 串串香 → 香 → 曰
- **definition:** say
- **pinyin:** yuē
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth, signifying speech
  - **interpretation:** The character 曰 (yuē, "say") visually resembles a mouth or an opening, symbolizing the action of speaking or saying something.
- **examples:**
  - 老师(師)曰：勤奋(奮)是成功之母。
    - Lǎoshī yuē：qínfèn shì chénggōng zhī mǔ。
    - The teacher said, 'Diligence is the mother of success.'
  - 孔子曰，学(學)而不思则(則)罔。
    - Kǒngzǐ yuē, xué ér bù sī zé wǎng。
    - Confucius said, 'Learning without thought leads to confusion.'
  - 老子曰，无(無)为(為)而治。
    - Lǎozǐ yuē, wúwéi ér zhì。
    - Laozi said, 'Governance should be achieved through non-action.'
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 曰](@media/glyph66f0.png)

## 秋葵
---
## okra
### qiū kuí
---
- **definition:** okra
- **pinyin:** qiū kuí
- **components:**
  - 秋
    - qiū
    - autumn
  - 葵
    - kuí
    - mallow
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 秋 (qiū, "autumn") 葵 (kuí, "mallow")
  - **interpretation:** The character 秋 (qiū, "autumn") reflects the harvest season, associated with crops reaching maturity, and identifies the time for harvesting many vegetables. 葵 (kuí, "mallow") represents okra as it belongs to the mallow family. Thus, 秋葵 (qiū kuí) describes okra as a plant that matures and is harvested around autumn, belonging to the mallow family.
- **examples:**
  - 秋葵是绿(綠)色的蔬菜。
    - Qiūkuí shì lǜsè de shūcài.
    - Okra is a green vegetable.
  - 我最喜欢(歡)炒秋葵。
    - Wǒ zuì xǐhuān chǎo qiūkuí.
    - I like fried okra the most.
  - 中餐时(時)，我们(們)吃了秋葵汤(湯)。
    - Zhōngcān shí, wǒmen chīle qiūkuí tāng.
    - During lunch, we had okra soup.
### 秋葵 → 秋
- **definition:** autumn
- **pinyin:** qiū
- **components:**
  - 禾
    - hé
    - grain
  - 火
    - huǒ
    - fire
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 禾 (hé, 'grain') + 火 (huǒ, 'fire') =
    - grain + fire ->
    - harvest time ->
    - autumn
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 'grain' and 'fire', symbolizing the practice of burning fields after harvest, marking autumn as harvest time.
- **examples:**
  - 秋天来(來)了。
    - Qiū tiān lái le.
    - Autumn has arrived.
  - 秋风(風)送爽，稻谷(穀)金黄(黃)。
    - Qiū fēng sòng shuǎng, dào gǔ jīn huáng.
    - The autumn breeze brings coolness, and the rice is golden.
  - 在秋季的午后，书(書)香满(滿)室。
    - Zài qiū jì de wǔ hòu, shū xiāng mǎn shì.
    - On an autumn afternoon, the room is filled with the fragrance of books.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 秋](@media/glyph79cb.png)
### 秋葵 → 秋 → 禾
- **definition:** grain
- **pinyin:** hé
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a stalk of grain or cereal plant
  - **interpretation:** The character 禾 (hé, 'grain') visually represents a plant with roots and leaves, focusing on the appearance of staple crops like rice or millet. This clearly conveys its meaning as it resembles the actual shape of a plant grown for its grain.
- **examples:**
  - 收获(穫)的禾香弥(彌)漫在田野中。
    - Shōuhuò de hé xiāng mímàn zài tiányě zhōng.
    - The fragrance of grain filled the fields.
  - 农(農)民辛勤耕作，收割禾穗。
    - Nóngmín xīnqín gēngzuò, shōugē hé suì.
    - The hardworking farmers harvested the ears of grain.
  - 春雨滋润(潤)了禾苗，预(預)示着(著)丰(豐)收。
    - Chūnyǔ zīrùn le hé miáo, yùshì zhe fēngshōu.
    - The spring rain nourished the grain seedlings, foreshadowing a bountiful harvest.

### 秋葵 → 秋 → 火
- **definition:** fire
- **pinyin:** huǒ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts flames rising from a fire
  - **interpretation:** The character 火 (huǒ, "fire") visually represents flames flickering upwards, which intuitively conveys the essence of fire. This simple depiction is an effective way to capture the dynamic and essential nature of fire.
- **examples:**
  - 火在壁炉(爐)中熊熊燃烧(燒)。
    - Huǒ zài bìlú zhōng xióngxióng ránshāo.
    - The fire burns fiercely in the fireplace.
  - 野外露营(營)时(時)，火能驱(驅)走寒冷。
    - Yěwài lùyíng shí, huǒ néng qūzǒu hánlěng.
    - When camping outdoors, the fire can drive away the cold.
  - 遇到火灾(災)时(時)，迅速疏散最为(為)重要。
    - Yù dào huǒzāi shí, xùnsù shū sàn zuìwéi zhòngyào.
    - In case of a fire, evacuating quickly is of utmost importance.

### 秋葵 → 葵
- **definition:** mallow
- **pinyin:** kuí
- **components:**
  - 艹
    - cǎo
    - grass; plant
  - 癸
    - guǐ
    - tenth heavenly stem
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 艹("grass; plant") + phonetic 癸(sound) ->
    - a kind of plant
  - **interpretation:** The character 葵 combines the semantic component 艹, indicating 'grass' or 'plant', with the phonetic component 癸, which provides the sound. This structure denotes a kind of plant, which can include mallow, sunflower, or hibiscus based on context.
- **examples:**
  - 花园(園)中种(種)满(滿)了向日葵。
    - Huāyuán zhōng zhòng mǎn le xiàngrìkuí.
    - The garden is filled with sunflowers.
  - 在古代，葵花常被用作药(藥)材。
    - Zài gǔdài, kuíhuā cháng bèi yòng zuò yàocái.
    - In ancient times, the mallow flower was often used as medicine.
  - 清晨的露水，使葵花显(顯)得更加美丽(麗)。
    - Qīngchén de lùshuǐ, shǐ kuíhuā xiǎnde gèngjiā měilì.
    - The morning dew makes the sunflower look even more beautiful.
### 秋葵 → 葵 → 艹
- **definition:** grass; plant
- **pinyin:** cǎo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts blades of grass
  - **interpretation:** 艹 is a pictogram representing grass or plants, resembling blades of grass. It is commonly used as a radical in other characters related to grass or vegetation.
- **examples:**
  - 他写(寫)字时(時)用艹作草字的偏旁。
    - Tā xiězì shí yòng cǎo zuò cǎozì de piānpáng.
    - He uses '艹' as the radical for grass in his characters.
  - 春天到来(來)时(時)，艹生长(長)得很快。
    - Chūntiān dàolái shí, cǎo shēngzhǎng de hěn kuài.
    - When spring arrives, grass grows rapidly.
### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸
- **definition:** tenth heavenly stem
- **pinyin:** guǐ
- **components:**
  - 戣
    - kuí
    - halberd
  - 葵
    - kuí
    - mallow
  - 規
    - guī
    - compass; rule
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 癸 depicts a form whose original meaning is uncertain ->
    - associated with measuring tools or setups for determining directions and solstices ->
    - possible original forms of 戣 (kuí, "halberd"), 葵 (kuí, "mallow"), 規 (guī, "compass; rule")
  - **interpretation:** The character 癸 (guǐ, "tenth earthly branch") is a pictogram whose depiction is uncertain but is conceptually linked to measurement or orientation tools. These tools were possibly used for solar observations or direction finding, thus lending the character significance in calendrical or positional contexts.
- **examples:**
  - 在中国(國)古代历(曆)法中，癸象征(徵)着(著)第十个(個)时(時)间(間)段。
    - Zài Zhōngguó gǔdài lìfǎ zhōng, guǐ xiàngzhēng zhe dì shí gè shíjiān duàn.
    - In traditional Chinese calendrical systems, guǐ symbolizes the tenth time period.
  - 古代学(學)者通过(過)观(觀)察天象，用癸来(來)记(記)录(錄)岁(歲)月更迭。
    - Gǔdài xuézhě tōngguò guānchá tiānxiàng, yòng guǐ lái jìlù suìyuè gēngdié.
    - Ancient scholars, by observing celestial phenomena, used guǐ to record the passage of time.
  - 天干地支系统(統)里，癸代表第十个(個)地支。
    - Tiāngān dìzhī xìtǒng lǐ, guǐ dàibiǎo dì shí gè dìzhī.
    - In the heavenly stems and earthly branches system, guǐ represents the tenth earthly branch.

### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 戣
- **definition:** halberd
- **pinyin:** kuí
- **components:**
  - 戈
    - gē
    - halberd
  - 魏
    - wèi
    - a Warring State; high
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 戈 (gē, "halberd") + phonetic 魏 (wèi) ->
    - sounding kuí, weapon type
  - **interpretation:** The character 戣 (kuí, "halberd") combines the semantic component 戈 (gē, "halberd") which directly refers to a type of weapon, with the phonetic component 魏 (wèi) to provide the sound kuí. The character specifically denotes a kind of halberd, inheriting its physical association from the戈 component.
### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 戣 → 戈
- **definition:** halberd
- **pinyin:** gē
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a spear or halberd, a type of weapon
  - **interpretation:** The character 戈(gē, 'spear') visually represents a spear or halberd, highlighting its function and importance as a weapon in ancient Chinese warfare.
- **examples:**
  - 古代战(戰)士持戈，勇闯(闖)敌(敵)营(營)。
    - Gǔdài zhànshì chí gē, yǒng chuǎng dí yíng.
    - Ancient warriors wielded the spear, bravely attacking the enemy camp.
  - 博物馆(館)珍藏古兵器，展厅(廳)陈(陳)列戈。
    - Bówùguǎn zhēncáng gǔ bīngqì, zhǎntīng chénliè gē.
    - The museum preserves ancient weapons, and the exhibition hall displays a spear.

### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 戣 → 魏
- **definition:** a Warring State; high
- **pinyin:** wèi
- **components:**
  - 委
    - wěi
    - entrust
  - 鬼
    - guǐ
    - ghost
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 委 + phonetic 鬼 ->
    - 魏
  - **interpretation:** The character 魏 (wèi), referring to the historical state, combines phonetic elements 委 (wěi, 'entrust') and 鬼 (guǐ, 'ghost'), with no direct semantic contribution from either component. The usage for the state of Wei relates primarily through phonetic borrowing rather than inherent meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 在战(戰)国(國)时(時)期，魏国(國)是七雄之一。
    - Zài Zhànguó shíqī, Wèiguó shì qīxióng zhī yī.
    - During the Warring States period, the State of Wei was one of the Seven Heroes.
  - 魏武王是一个(個)有名的统(統)治者。
    - Wèi Wǔ Wáng shì yī gè yǒumíng de tǒngzhìzhě.
    - King Wei Wu was a famous ruler.
  - 这(這)个(個)山峰耸(聳)立在云(雲)端之上，显(顯)得格外雄伟(偉)。
    - Zhège shānfēng sǒnglì zài yúnduān zhī shàng, xiǎnde géwài xióngwěi.
    - This mountain peak stands tall above the clouds, appearing exceptionally majestic.
### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 戣 → 魏 → 委
- **definition:** entrust
- **pinyin:** wěi
- **components:**
  - 禾
    - hé
    - grain
  - 女
    - nǚ
    - woman
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 禾 (hé, "grain") + semantic 女 (nǚ, "woman") ->
    - entrust
  - **interpretation:** The character 委 combines 禾 (hé, "grain") as the phonetic component to suggest sound, with 女 (nǚ, "woman") as the semantic component. Originally, the oracle bone representation used 𠃊, depicting a figure kneeling, which aligns with the idea of yielding or resigning. Hence, the combination implies entrusting or assigning a task, as one might with a trusted companion or subordinate.
- **examples:**
  - 我把重要的任务(務)委托(託)给(給)他。
    - Wǒ bǎ zhòngyào de rènwù wěituō gěi tā.
    - I entrusted the important task to him.
  - 经(經)理委任了一名新助理。
    - Jīnglǐ wěirèn le yī míng xīn zhùlǐ.
    - The manager appointed a new assistant.
  - 她被公司委以重任。
    - Tā bèi gōngsī wěi yǐ zhòngrèn.
    - She was entrusted with significant responsibilities by the company.

### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 戣 → 魏 → 鬼
- **definition:** ghost
- **pinyin:** guǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a kneeling man or figure with an ugly face (甶) + small 厶 (trace of tail) added later
  - **interpretation:** The character 鬼 (guǐ, "demon") visually represents a kneeling figure with a distinctive, mask-like face, evoking the image of a supernatural being or ghost. The addition of a small 厶 suggests a residual tail, enhancing its demon-like appearance. This depiction highlights the character's association with eerie, otherworldly entities.
- **examples:**
  - 深夜独(獨)行时(時)，忽遇鬼影飘(飄)忽。
    - Shēnyè dúxíng shí, hū yù guǐ yǐng piāohū.
    - Walking alone in the deep night, suddenly encountering a fleeting ghostly silhouette.
  - 村里(裡)流传(傳)故事说(說)鬼出没(沒)，人们(們)夜半小心提灯(燈)。
    - Cūn lǐ liúchuán gùshì shuō guǐ chūmò, rénmen yèbàn xiǎoxīn tí dēng.
    - Stories circulate in the village that demons haunt the area, so people cautiously carry lanterns at midnight.

### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 規
- **definition:** compass; rule
- **pinyin:** guī
- **components:**
  - 夫
    - fū
    - husband
  - 癸
    - guǐ
    - tenth heavenly stem
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - Originally a pictogram of a compass ->
    - transformed to combine 夫 (fū, "husband") + a phonetic component similar to 癸
  - **interpretation:** The character 規 (guī, "compass") originally depicted a cross-shaped measuring compass. Over time, it evolved to incorporate elements for phonetic reasons—specifically, adopting an abbreviated form of the phonetic component 癸 (guǐ, "tenth heavenly stem"). The association with 夫 (fū, "husband") originally related to the tool-like function of a compass in measurement.
  - **simplification:** 规(規): 見 component was removed and replaced with 见, a simpler form, preserving the phonetic similarity.
- **examples:**
  - 老师(師)教我们(們)如何使用规(規)。
    - Lǎoshī jiāo wǒmen rúhé shǐyòng guī.
    - The teacher teaches us how to use a compass.
  - 建筑(築)师(師)利用规(規)和尺来(來)绘(繪)制(製)蓝(藍)图(圖)。
    - Jiànzhùshī lìyòng guī hé chǐ lái huìzhì lántú.
    - The architect uses a compass and ruler to draft blueprints.
  - 古代的工匠依靠简(簡)单(單)的规(規)和工具制(製)作精美的器物。
    - Gǔdài de gōngjiàng yīkào jiǎndān de guī hé gōngjù zhìzuò jīngměi de qìwù.
    - Ancient artisans relied on simple compasses and tools to craft exquisite artifacts.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 規](@media/glyph898f.png)
### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 規 → 夫
- **definition:** husband
- **pinyin:** fū
- **components:**
  - 大
    - dà
    - big
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a variant form of 大 (dà, "big") representing an adult man with a hairpin ->
    - became associated with 夫 (fū, "man").
  - **interpretation:** 夫 (fū, "man") was visually similar to 大 (dà, "big") and was originally interchangeable. The addition of the horizontal stroke was interpreted as a hairpin, symbolizing adulthood for men.
- **examples:**
  - 此夫心怀(懷)大志。
    - Cǐ fū xīn huái dà zhì.
    - This man has lofty aspirations.
  - 他勤劳(勞)努力，堪称(稱)良夫。
    - Tā qín láo nǔ lì, kān chēng liáng fū.
    - He works diligently and is regarded as an exemplary man.
- **historical forms:**

### 秋葵 → 葵 → 癸 → 規 → 夫 → 大
- **definition:** big
- **pinyin:** dà
- **components:**
  - 夫
    - fū
    - man
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a person facing forward ->
    - Borrowed phonetically for 'big'; original form of 夫 (fū, 'man')
  - **interpretation:** The character 大(dà) depicts a person facing forward, representing 'big' by suggesting the idea of someone standing prominently. Although often thought of as a person with outstretched arms, early scripts do not support this interpretation. It was originally the form of 夫 (fū, 'man') and was later phonetically borrowed for the meaning 'big.'
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)个(個)房子很大。
    - Zhè ge fángzi hěn dà.
    - This house is very big.
  - 大海波涛(濤)汹(洶)涌(湧)，展现(現)出大自然的力量。
    - Dàhǎi bōtāo xiōngyǒng, zhǎnxiàn chū dàzìrán de lìliàng.
    - The vast ocean waves surge, showcasing the power of nature.
  - 大人物登场(場)，留下传(傳)奇。
    - Dà rénwù dēngchǎng, liúxià chuánqí.
    - Great figures make an appearance, leaving behind legends.
- **historical forms:**

## 粉红(紅)玫瑰
---
## pink rose
### fěn hóng méi guī
---
- **traditional:** 粉紅玫瑰
- **definition:** pink rose
- **pinyin:** fěn hóng méi guī
- **components:**
  - 粉紅
    - fěnhóng
    - pink
  - 玫瑰
    - méiguī
    - rose
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 粉 (fěn, "powder; pink") and 紅 (hóng, "red") together form 粉紅 (fěnhóng, "pink"), indicating the light shade of red. 玫瑰 (méiguī, "rose") refers to the flower.
  - **interpretation:** The term 粉紅 (fěnhóng, "pink") combines 粉 (fěn, "powder") to imply a softer, lighter version of 紅 (hóng, "red"), creating the pastel color pink. 玫瑰 (méiguī, "rose") refers to the flower known for its association with romance and beauty. Together, 粉紅玫瑰 (fěnhóng méiguī, "pink rose") evokes the image of a rose colored in a gentle shade of pink.
- **examples:**
  - 她收到了很多粉红(紅)玫瑰。
    - Tā shōu dào le hěn duō fěn hóng méi guī.
    - She received many pink roses.
  - 粉红(紅)玫瑰的香味令人陶醉。
    - Fěn hóng méi guī de xiāngwèi lìng rén táozuì.
    - The fragrance of pink roses is intoxicating.
  - 在花园(園)里(裡)，粉红(紅)玫瑰盛开(開)的时(時)候，令人感到无(無)比幸福。
    - Zài huāyuán lǐ, fěn hóng méi guī shèngkāi de shíhòu, lìng rén gǎndào wúbǐ xìngfú.
    - In the garden, when the pink roses are in full bloom, it brings incomparable happiness.
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 粉紅
- **definition:** pink
- **pinyin:** fěnhóng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:**
    - 粉 (fěn, "powder") + 紅 (hóng, "red") =
    - powdery red ->
    - pink
  - **interpretation:** The term 粉紅(fěnhóng) derives its meaning from combining 粉 (fěn, "powder"), which evokes a sense of lightness and dilution, with 紅 (hóng, "red"), which provides the base color. The combination suggests a red that has been lightened or softened into a pink hue, akin to the appearance of red when mixed with white powder.
- **examples:**
  - 我喜欢(歡)粉红(紅)色的花。
    - Wǒ xǐhuān fěnhóng sè de huā.
    - I like pink flowers.
  - 她穿了一件粉红(紅)裙子。
    - Tā chuānle yī jiàn fěnhóng qúnzi.
    - She wore a pink dress.
  - 这(這)面墙(牆)是粉红(紅)色的，感觉(覺)很温(溫)暖。
    - Zhè miàn qiáng shì fěnhóng sè de, gǎnjué hěn wēnnuǎn.
    - This wall is pink, and it feels very warm.
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 粉紅 → 紅
- **definition:** red; popular; revolution; bonus
- **pinyin:** hóng
- **components:**
  - 糸
    - mì
    - silk
  - 工
    - gōng
    - work
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 糸 (mì, "silk") + phonetic 工 (gōng) ->
    - red
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 糸 (mì, "silk"), illustrating the context of dyed or colored silk, with the phonetic 工 (gōng), offering the pronunciation. The use of silk relates to the traditional skill of dyeing fabric, specifically producing the color red.
  - **simplification:** Simplified as 红, where 糸 (mì, "silk") was replaced by the simplified radical 纟, reducing strokes while keeping the character's meaning intact.
- **examples:**
  - 他的脸(臉)红(紅)了。
    - Tā de liǎn hóng le.
    - His face turned red.
  - 这(這)本书(書)最近很红(紅)。
    - Zhè běn shū zuìjìn hěn hóng.
    - This book is very popular recently.
  - 在革命时(時)期，许(許)多人都穿着(著)红(紅)色的服装(裝)。
    - Zài gémìng shíqí, xǔduō rén dōu chuānzhe hóngsè de fúzhuāng.
    - During the revolutionary period, many people wore red clothing.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 紅](@media/glyph7d05.png)
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 粉紅 → 紅 → 糸
- **definition:** silk
- **pinyin:** mì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a skein of silk
  - **interpretation:** The character 糸(mì, "silk; thread") represents a pictorial representation of a skein of silk, visually capturing the concept of thread or fiber.
- **examples:**
  - 她手工制(製)作了一条(條)漂亮的丝(絲)巾。
    - Tā shǒugōng zhìzuòle yī tiáo piàoliang de sī jīn.
    - She handcrafted a beautiful silk scarf.
  - 这(這)个(個)设(設)计(計)图(圖)必须(須)用细(細)糸画(畫)出来(來)。
    - Zhège shèjìtú bìxū yòng xì mì huà chūlái.
    - This design drawing must be sketched with fine thread.
  - 我们(們)参(參)观(觀)了古代的织(織)布技术(術)，对(對)丝(絲)绸(綢)制(製)作产(產)生了兴(興)趣。
    - Wǒmen cānguānle gǔdài de zhībù jìshù, duì sīchóu zhìzuò chǎnshēngle xìngqù.
    - We visited ancient weaving techniques and developed an interest in silk production.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 糸](@media/glyph7cf8.png)
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 粉紅 → 紅 → 工
- **definition:** work
- **pinyin:** gōng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a bladed tool to plow the ground and to mark a border, or a carpenter's square
  - **interpretation:** 工 (gōng, "work") represents either a tool used in agriculture for marking or a carpenter's square, reflecting its connection to traditional manual labor and craftsmanship.
- **examples:**
  - 他每天下午去做工。
    - Tā měitiān xiàwǔ qù zuò gōng.
    - He goes to work every afternoon.
  - 工厂(廠)里(裡)的机(機)器不停地运(運)转(轉)。
    - Gōng chǎng lǐ de jīqì bù tíng de yùnzhuǎn.
    - The machines in the factory run nonstop.
  - 这(這)位工人技艺(藝)精湛。
    - Zhè wèi gōngrén jìyì jīngzhàn.
    - This worker is highly skilled.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 工](@media/glyph5de5.png)
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 玫瑰
- **definition:** rose
- **pinyin:** méiguī
- **components:**
  - 玫
    - méi
    - rose gemstone; beautiful small stone
  - 瑰
    - guī
    - rare; precious; exceptional
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 玫 (méi, "rose gemstone; beautiful small stone") has a historical association with something small, precious, and beautiful, similar to a gemstone. 瑰 (guī, "rare; precious; exceptional") emphasizes uniqueness and value, often referring to something remarkable or extraordinary. Together, 玫瑰 (méiguī, "rose") evokes the image of a precious and exceptionally beautiful flower.
  - **interpretation:** 玫 (méi, "rose gemstone; beautiful small stone") focuses on beauty and preciousness, suggesting something delicate and charming like a gemstone. 瑰 (guī, "rare; precious; exceptional") highlights the unique and extraordinary qualities of the rose, marking it as a rare flower of great beauty. The combination implies an exquisite, highly valued flower—like a 'gem among flowers', hence the concept of a rose.
- **examples:**
  - 玫瑰花开(開)得很美。
    - Méi guī huā kāi de hěn měi.
    - The rose blooms beautifully.
  - 她收到了一束红(紅)玫瑰。
    - Tā shōu dào le yī shù hóng méi guī.
    - She received a bouquet of red roses.
  - 玫瑰象征(徵)爱(愛)情。
    - Méi guī xiàng zhēng ài qíng.
    - Roses symbolize love.
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 玫瑰 → 玫
- **definition:** rose gemstone; beautiful small stone
- **pinyin:** méi
- **components:**
  - 𤣩
    - (jade
    - a type of jade
  - 文
    - wén
    - script; pattern
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:** semantic 𤣩 (jade) + phonetic 文 (sound)
  - **interpretation:** 玫 (méi) combines the semantic 𤣩, meaning "jade," with the phonetic component 文 (wén) to convey the sound. The character is used to denote a type of jade, leveraging 𤣩 to evoke the preciousness and craftsmanship associated with jade.
- **examples:**
  - 她戴了一串玫玉项(項)链(鏈)。
    - Tā dài le yī chuàn méi yù xiàngliàn.
    - She wore a necklace with rose jade.
  - 玫石被雕刻成精美的饰(飾)品。
    - Méi shí bèi diāokè chéng jīngměi de shìpǐn.
    - The rose jade was carved into exquisite ornaments.
  - 这(這)种(種)玫石在市场(場)上非常受欢(歡)迎。
    - Zhè zhǒng méi shí zài shìchǎng shàng fēicháng shòu huānyíng.
    - This type of rose jade is very popular in the market.
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 玫瑰 → 玫 → 𤣩
- **definition:** a type of jade
- **pinyin:** (jade
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a cong (ritual jade totem)
  - **interpretation:** The character 𤣩 is a variant form of 玉 (yù, "jade"), which originally depicted a cong, a type of ritual jade totem. Over time, a dot was added to distinguish it from 王 (wáng, "king") due to the visual similarity between the two characters. Jade played a significant role in art and rituals, which is why its pictogram was distinctly designed. The character represents the material jade and its cultural significance as a precious and spiritual object.
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 玫瑰 → 玫 → 文
- **definition:** script; pattern
- **pinyin:** wén
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a crested animal pattern, representing patterns of writing.
  - **interpretation:** 文 (wén, 'language; culture') originally depicted a symbol or pattern on objects, which is closely related to text and writing as forms of patterned representation, embodying cultural expression.
- **examples:**
  - 他研究古文。
    - Tā yánjiū gǔwén.
    - He studies classical literature.
  - 我们(們)的文化深厚，文学(學)绵(綿)长(長)悠远(遠)。
    - Wǒmen de wénhuà shēnhòu, wénxué miáncháng yōuyuǎn.
    - Our culture is profound, and our literature is long and far-reaching.
  - 书(書)中蕴(蘊)含丰(豐)厚的文采。
    - Shū zhōng yùnhán fēnghòu de wéncǎi.
    - The book is imbued with rich literary elegance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 文](@media/glyph6587.png)
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 玫瑰 → 瑰
- **definition:** rare; precious; exceptional
- **pinyin:** guī
- **components:**
  - 𤣩
    - yù
    - jade
  - 鬼
    - guǐ
    - ghost
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 𤣩 (jade) + phonetic 鬼 ->
    - extraordinary; precious
  - **interpretation:** 瑰 uses 𤣩 (jade) to signify something valuable and beautiful, with 鬼 contributing the sound. Jade, being a precious stone, naturally leads to the meaning 'precious.' The phonetic 鬼 does not contribute meaning here but provides the pronunciation, guiding the sense of 'extraordinary' as being distinct or remarkable, much like the unique and distinguished nature of precious jade.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)些宝(寶)石看起来(來)非常瑰丽(麗)。
    - Zhèxiē bǎoshí kàn qǐlái fēicháng guīlì.
    - These gemstones look extremely precious.
  - 她拥(擁)有一种(種)瑰丽(麗)的想象力，总(總)是能创(創)造出非凡的作品。
    - Tā yǒngyǒu yī zhǒng guīlì de xiǎngxiàng lì, zǒng shì néng chuàngzào chū fēifán de zuòpǐn.
    - She possesses an extraordinary imagination and is always able to create remarkable works.
  - 那幅画(畫)展现(現)了自然的瑰丽(麗)与(與)宁(寧)静(靜)。
    - Nà fú huà zhǎnxiàn le zìrán de guīlì yǔ níngjìng.
    - The painting showcases the preciousness and tranquility of nature.
### 粉红(紅)玫瑰 → 玫瑰 → 瑰 → 鬼
- **definition:** ghost
- **pinyin:** guǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a kneeling man or figure with an ugly face (甶) + small 厶 (trace of tail) added later
  - **interpretation:** The character 鬼 (guǐ, "demon") visually represents a kneeling figure with a distinctive, mask-like face, evoking the image of a supernatural being or ghost. The addition of a small 厶 suggests a residual tail, enhancing its demon-like appearance. This depiction highlights the character's association with eerie, otherworldly entities.
- **examples:**
  - 深夜独(獨)行时(時)，忽遇鬼影飘(飄)忽。
    - Shēnyè dúxíng shí, hū yù guǐ yǐng piāohū.
    - Walking alone in the deep night, suddenly encountering a fleeting ghostly silhouette.
  - 村里(裡)流传(傳)故事说(說)鬼出没(沒)，人们(們)夜半小心提灯(燈)。
    - Cūn lǐ liúchuán gùshì shuō guǐ chūmò, rénmen yèbàn xiǎoxīn tí dēng.
    - Stories circulate in the village that demons haunt the area, so people cautiously carry lanterns at midnight.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 鬼](@media/glyph9b3c.png)

## 粽子
---
## rice dumpling
### zòng zi
---
- **definition:** rice dumpling
- **pinyin:** zòng zi
- **components:**
  - 粽
    - zòng
    - sticky rice wrapped in bamboo leaves
  - 子
    - zi
    - child; small thing
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 粽 (zòng, "sticky rice wrapped in bamboo leaves"), 子 (zi, "child; small thing")
  - **interpretation:** 粽 (zòng, "sticky rice wrapped in bamboo leaves") refers directly to the traditional food item of sticky rice cooked in leaves. 子 (zi, "child; small thing") is often used in Chinese to denote a small or compact version of an object, essentially referring to a 'dumpling' or small parcel of food. Putting these together, 粽子 refers to the dish known as a rice dumpling, small packages of sticky rice encased in leaves, especially popular during the Dragon Boat Festival.
- **examples:**
  - 端午节(節)的时(時)候，我们(們)吃粽子。
    - Duānwǔ jié de shíhòu, wǒmen chī zòngzi.
    - During the Dragon Boat Festival, we eat rice dumplings.
  - 她亲(親)手包了很多粽子。
    - Tā qīnshǒu bāo le hěn duō zòngzi.
    - She made many rice dumplings by hand.
  - 粽子有甜的，也有咸(鹹)的。
    - Zòngzi yǒu tián de, yě yǒu xián de.
    - Rice dumplings can be sweet or savory.
### 粽子 → 粽(糉)
- **traditional:** 糉
- **definition:** sticky rice wrapped in bamboo leaves
- **pinyin:** zòng
- **components:**
  - 米
    - mǐ
    - rice
  - 㚇
    - zōng
    - carefree, easygoing
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 米 (mǐ, "rice") + phonetic 㚇 (zōng) ->
    - sticky rice wrapped in leaves
  - **interpretation:** The character 糉 originated as a phono-semantic compound where 米 (mǐ, "rice") indicates the semantic field relevant to rice, and 㚇 (zōng) provides the sound. Together they denote sticky rice wrapped in leaves, commonly referred to as 粽子 (zòngzi) in modern usage.
- **examples:**
  - 我喜欢(歡)在端午节(節)吃粽(糉)子。
    - Wǒ xǐhuān zài duānwǔjié chī zòngzi.
    - I like to eat sticky rice wrapped in leaves during the Dragon Boat Festival.
  - 她在市场(場)上买(買)了很多粽(糉)子。
    - Tā zài shìchǎng shàng mǎile hěn duō zòngzi.
    - She bought a lot of sticky rice wrapped in leaves at the market.
  - 粽(糉)子的味道让(讓)我想起了童年。
    - Zòngzi de wèidào ràng wǒ xiǎngqǐle tóngnián.
    - The taste of sticky rice wrapped in leaves reminds me of my childhood.
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 米
- **definition:** rice
- **pinyin:** mǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts rice kernels ->
    - 米(mǐ, 'rice')
  - **interpretation:** The character 米(mǐ, 'rice') visually represents dehusked rice kernels to differentiate it from 粟. The horizontal stroke may symbolize a bamboo sieve, emphasizing the process of separating grains from their husks.
- **examples:**
  - 我喜欢(歡)吃米饭(飯)。
    - Wǒ xǐhuān chī mǐfàn.
    - I like to eat rice.
  - 她从(從)农(農)村带(帶)回一袋米，用来(來)煮饭(飯)。
    - Tā cóng nóngcūn dài huí yī dài mǐ, yòng lái zhǔ fàn.
    - She brought a bag of rice from the countryside to cook.
  - 市场(場)上有新米出售。
    - Shìchǎng shàng yǒu xīn mǐ chūshòu.
    - New rice is available in the market.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 米](@media/glyph7c73.png)
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 㚇
- **definition:** carefree, easygoing
- **pinyin:** zōng
- **components:**
  - 子
    - zǐ
    - child
  - 乑
    - yín
    - together
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 子 (zǐ, "child") + 乑 (yín, "together") =
    - a group of carefree, lighthearted children playing together ->
    - carefree, easygoing
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 子 (zǐ, "child") with 乑 (yín, "together"), giving the image of children playing together uninhibitedly, capturing the essence of being carefree and easygoing.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 㚇](@media/glyph3687.png)
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 㚇 → 子
- **definition:** child
- **pinyin:** zǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a baby with a large head and spread arms, with legs wrapped in a blanket
  - **interpretation:** The character 子(zǐ, "child") is a pictorial representation of a baby, emphasizing characteristics like a large head and outstretched arms typical of infants, which conveys the essence of a child. This visual element helps infer its meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)小子很调(調)皮。
    - Zhè xiǎo zǐ hěn tiáopí.
    - This kid is very naughty.
  - 他的小子爱(愛)打篮(籃)球，每天都锻(鍛)炼(煉)身体(體)。
    - Tā de xiǎo zǐ ài dǎ lánqiú, měitiān dōu duànliàn shēntǐ.
    - His child loves playing basketball, and practices every day.
  - 孤独(獨)的子需要关(關)爱(愛)。
    - Gūdú de zǐ xūyào guān'ài.
    - A lonely child needs care.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 子](@media/glyph5b50.png)
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 㚇 → 乑
- **definition:** together
- **pinyin:** yín
- **components:**
  - 眾
    - zhòng
    - multitude
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a sun (日) above three humans (㐺) ->
    - sun modified to resemble a horizontal eye (early form of 目) ->
    - a crowd under someone’s gaze ->
    - final form resembles 罒.
  - **interpretation:** The character 乑 is derived from 眾(众) (zhòng, "multitude"), symbolizing a crowd gathered under the gaze of the sun, reinterpreted as the eye of authority overseeing a collective group, representing the concept of 'together' or 'gathered'.
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 㚇 → 乑 → 眾
- **definition:** multitude
- **pinyin:** zhòng
- **components:**
  - 日
    - rì
    - sun
  - 人
    - rén
    - person
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 日(日, "sun") above three 人(人, "person") ->
    - sun over a crowd ->
    - modified to 罒(resembles "eye") + three 人(人, "person") ->
    - crowd under gaze
  - **interpretation:** The character originally depicted the sun shining over three figures, indicating people gathered or working outdoors. This was modified over time with the top element stylized to resemble an eye watching over a crowd, symbolizing a multitude under observation.
- **examples:**
  - 人群聚集在广(廣)场(場)上，引起了围(圍)观(觀)者的注意。
    - Rénqún jùjí zài guǎngchǎng shàng, yǐnqǐle wéiguān zhě de zhùyì.
    - The crowd gathered in the square, attracting the attention of onlookers.
  - 市长(長)在大会(會)上向群众(眾)发(發)表了讲(講)话(話)。
    - Shìzhǎng zài dàhuì shàng xiàng qúnzhòng fābiǎo le jiǎnghuà.
    - The mayor delivered a speech to the multitude at the conference.
  - 为(為)了满(滿)足大众(眾)的需求，公司推出了新产(產)品。
    - Wèile mǎnzú dàzhòng de xūqiú, gōngsī tuīchū le xīn chǎnpǐn.
    - To meet the needs of the multitude, the company launched a new product.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 眾](@media/glyph773e.png)
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 㚇 → 乑 → 眾 → 日
- **definition:** sun
- **pinyin:** rì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts the sun; a dot or line added in the center to distinguish from similar characters e.g. 囗
  - **interpretation:** As a pictogram, 日(rì, 'sun') directly represents the sun. In ancient times, the added dot helped visually differentiate it from other characters. This is analogous to the astronomical symbol ☉ and Egyptian hieroglyph 𓇳, both depicting the sun.
- **examples:**
  - 晨曦来(來)临(臨)时(時)，日出东(東)方。
    - Chénxī láilín shí, rìchū dōngfāng.
    - At the break of dawn, the sun rises in the east.
  - 温(溫)暖的日光洒(灑)满(滿)大地。
    - Wēnnuǎn de rìguāng sǎ mǎn dàdì.
    - The warm sunlight spreads over the earth.
  - 中午时(時)分，日高挂(掛)天。
    - Zhōngwǔ shífēn, rì gāo guà tiān.
    - At noon, the sun hangs high in the sky.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 日](@media/glyph65e5.png)
### 粽子 → 粽(糉) → 㚇 → 乑 → 眾 → 人
- **definition:** person
- **pinyin:** rén
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts side view of a standing man, highlighting an arm and a leg ->
    - visual representation of a person
  - **interpretation:** The character 人 (rén, 'person') effectively uses simple lines to depict the essential form of a human, making it immediately recognizable and intuitive as meaning 'person.'
- **examples:**
  - 他是个(個)好人。
    - Tā shì gè hǎo rén.
    - He is a good person.
  - 每个(個)人都有责(責)任，为(為)社会(會)作出贡(貢)献(獻)。
    - Měi gè rén dōu yǒu zérèn, wèi shèhuì zuòchū gòngxiàn.
    - Every person has a responsibility to contribute to society.
  - 人在旅途中，心灵(靈)获(獲)得了成长(長)。
    - Rén zài lǚtú zhōng, xīnlíng huòdé le chéngzhǎng.
    - People gain growth along their journey.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 人](@media/glyph4eba.png)
### 粽子 → 子
- **definition:** child; small thing
- **pinyin:** zi
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a baby with a large head and spread arms, with legs wrapped in a blanket
  - **interpretation:** The character 子(zǐ, "child") is a pictorial representation of a baby, emphasizing characteristics like a large head and outstretched arms typical of infants, which conveys the essence of a child. This visual element helps infer its meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)小子很调(調)皮。
    - Zhè xiǎo zǐ hěn tiáopí.
    - This kid is very naughty.
  - 他的小子爱(愛)打篮(籃)球，每天都锻(鍛)炼(煉)身体(體)。
    - Tā de xiǎo zǐ ài dǎ lánqiú, měitiān dōu duànliàn shēntǐ.
    - His child loves playing basketball, and practices every day.
  - 孤独(獨)的子需要关(關)爱(愛)。
    - Gūdú de zǐ xūyào guān'ài.
    - A lonely child needs care.

## 网(網)易
---
## NetEase
### Wǎng Yì
---
- **traditional:** 網易
- **definition:** NetEase
- **pinyin:** Wǎng Yì
- **components:**
  - 网(網)
    - wǎng
    - net
  - 易
    - yì
    - easy; exchange
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 網 (wǎng, "net") + 易 (yì, "easy; exchange") form the name of the Chinese internet technology company NetEase. The name suggests the company's foundational focus on internet technology and the concept of facilitating interactions or exchanges online.
  - **interpretation:** The combination of 網 (wǎng, "net"), referring to the internet, and 易 (yì, "easy"), implies a focus on simplifying and facilitating online interactions, aligning with NetEase's core business in internet services.
  - **simplification:** 網易 is simplified to 网易.
- **examples:**
  - 网(網)易是一家知名的互联(聯)网(網)公司。
    - Wǎng Yì shì yī jiā zhīmíng de hùliánwǎng gōngsī.
    - NetEase is a well-known internet company.
  - 我常使用网(網)易邮(郵)箱。
    - Wǒ cháng shǐyòng Wǎng Yì yóuxiāng.
    - I often use NetEase Mail.
  - 网(網)易产(產)品不断(斷)更新，满(滿)足用户(戶)需求。
    - Wǎng Yì chǎnpǐn bùduàn gēngxīn, mǎnzú yònghù xūqiú.
    - NetEase's products are continuously updated, meeting the needs of users.
### 网(網)易 → 网(網)
- **traditional:** 網
- **definition:** net
- **pinyin:** wǎng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a net with crossing lines or mesh ->
    - symbol for 'net'
  - **interpretation:** The character 网(網) (wǎng, 'net') visually represents a net with lines intersecting to form a grid, making it intuitive as a symbol for a net or mesh.
  - **simplification:** The simplified character 网 (wǎng) retains the essential visual structure of intersecting lines to depict a net. It conveys the idea of a net through a simplified representation without additional semantic or phonetic elements.
- **examples:**
  - 他用网(網)捕鱼(魚)，快乐(樂)满(滿)怀(懷)。
    - Tā yòng wǎng bǔ yú, kuàilè mǎn huái.
    - He fishes with a net and is full of joy.
  - 很多信息通过(過)网(網)传(傳)播，速度惊(驚)人。
    - Hěn duō xìnxī tōngguò wǎng chuánbō, sùdù jīngrén.
    - A lot of information spreads through the net with astonishing speed.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 网](@media/glyph7f51.png)
### 网(網)易 → 易
- **definition:** easy; exchange
- **pinyin:** yì
- **components:**
  - 賜
    - cì
    - bestow
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a filled container ->
    - original form of 賜 (cì, "bestow") ->
    - borrowed phonetically for "easy"
  - **interpretation:** The character 易(yì) depicts a filled container, symbolizing an act of bestowing, as seen in the original meaning of 賜 (cì, "bestow"). Over time, it was borrowed for the phonetic element to mean "easy," as the idea of a full or overflowing container could imply abundance or lack of difficulty.
- **examples:**
  - 学(學)习(習)新的语(語)言并(並)不容易。
    - Xuéxí xīn de yǔyán bìng bù róngyì.
    - Learning a new language is not easy.
  - 这(這)个(個)市场(場)可以交换(換)商品。
    - Zhège shìchǎng kěyǐ jiāohuàn shāngpǐn.
    - This market allows for the exchange of goods.
  - 解决(決)这(這)个(個)问(問)题(題)并(並)不容易，我们(們)需要团(團)队(隊)合作。
    - Jiějué zhège wèntí bìng bù róngyì, wǒmen xūyào tuánduì hézuò.
    - Solving this problem is not easy; we need team collaboration.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 易](@media/glyph6613.png)
### 网(網)易 → 易 → 賜
- **definition:** bestow
- **pinyin:** cì
- **components:**
  - 貝
    - bèi
    - shell; money
  - 易
    - yì
    - filled container
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 貝 (bèi, "shell, money") + phonetic 易 (yì, "filled container") ->
    - bestow
  - **interpretation:** 貝 (bèi, "shell, money") symbolizes valuables or treasures, while 易 (yì, "filled container") provides the sound. Together, they depict the act of granting or bestowing valuables or benefits onto someone, which is closely associated with giving gifts or rewards.
  - **simplification:** In the simplified form 赐(賜), the component 貝 (bèi) was simplified to 贝(貝), reducing the number of strokes.
- **examples:**
  - 国(國)王赐(賜)给(給)了他一件珍贵(貴)的礼(禮)物。
    - Guówáng cì gěi le tā yī jiàn zhēnguì de lǐwù.
    - The king bestowed upon him a precious gift.
  - 神明赐(賜)予我们(們)好运(運)。
    - Shénmíng cì yǔ wǒmen hǎoyùn.
    - The deities bestowed good fortune upon us.
  - 他希望上天能赐(賜)给(給)他智慧。
    - Tā xīwàng shàngtiān néng cì gěi tā zhìhuì.
    - He hopes that the heavens will bestow wisdom upon him.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 賜](@media/glyph8cdc.png)
### 网(網)易 → 易 → 賜 → 貝
- **definition:** shell; money
- **pinyin:** bèi
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a cowrie shell ->
    - used as currency in ancient China ->
    - stylized as 貝
  - **interpretation:** The character 貝(bèi, 'shell/money') visually represents a cowrie shell, which was used as a form of currency in ancient China. This explains why it is associated with money or valuables.
  - **simplification:** 贝 is a cursive script simplification of 貝, transforming the character into a more streamlined form while retaining its essence.
- **examples:**
  - 他把贝(貝)当作护(護)身符，放在口袋里(裡)。
    - Tā bǎ bèi dāng zuò hùshēn fú, fàng zài kǒudài lǐ.
    - He uses shells as a talisman, placing them in his pocket.
  - 古代人用贝(貝)作为(為)货(貨)币(幣)。
    - Gǔdài rén yòng bèi zuòwéi huòbì.
    - In ancient times, people used shells as currency.

## 茅台(臺)

## Moutai liquor
### máo tái
---
- **traditional:** 茅臺
- **definition:** Moutai liquor
- **pinyin:** máo tái
- **components:**
  - 茅
    - máo
    - reeds; grass
  - 台(臺)
    - tái
    - platform; stage
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 茅 (máo, "reeds") refers to a type of grass, which might have been abundant or distinctive in the geographical area. 臺(台) (tái, "platform") can refer to a flat area or a place of significance. In this compound, it forms the name of the place 茅台 (Máotáitáij, "Moutai"), which is famous for its liquor.
  - **interpretation:** 茅 (máo, "reeds") and 臺(台) (tái, "platform") together specify a particular geographical setting associated with the production of high-quality liquor. This compound strictly represents a place name, famously associated with 茅臺(台)酒 (Máotái jiǔ), a type of distilled Chinese liquor. The name suggests a unique locality or community known for its skilled liquor production, akin to terroir in winemaking.
- **examples:**
  - 茅台是一种(種)非常著名的中国(國)白酒。
    - Máotái shì yī zhǒng fēicháng zhùmíng de Zhōngguó báijiǔ.
    - Moutai is a very famous Chinese spirit.
  - 在婚宴上，他们(們)总(總)会(會)喝茅台。
    - Zài hūnyàn shàng, tāmen zǒng huì hē máotái.
    - At weddings, they always drink Moutai.
  - 他收藏了许(許)多不同年份的茅台。
    - Tā shōucángle xǔduō bùtóng niánfèn de máotái.
    - He has collected many different vintages of Moutai.
### 茅台(臺) → 茅
- **definition:** reeds; grass
- **pinyin:** máo
- **components:**
  - 艹
    - cǎo
    - plant
  - 矛
    - máo
    - spear
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 艹 (cǎo, "plant") + phonetic 矛 (máo, "spear") =
    - grass with long, pointed shape ->
    - cogon grass
  - **interpretation:** The character 茅(máo) conveys its meaning as cogon grass through the plant radical 艹 (cǎo, "plant") to signify vegetation, while 矛 (máo, "spear") suggests its long, sharp shape.
- **examples:**
  - 村里(裡)的人们(們)用茅盖(蓋)房子。
    - Cūn lǐ de rénmen yòng máo gài fángzi.
    - The villagers use cogon grass to thatch their houses.
  - 那间(間)茅屋充满(滿)古朴(樸)气(氣)息。
    - Nà jiān máo wū chōngmǎn gǔpǔ qìxī.
    - That cogon grass hut is full of rustic charm.
  - 村庄(莊)外的山坡上长(長)满(滿)了茅。
    - Cūnzhuāng wài de shānpō shàng zhǎngmǎn le máo.
    - The hillside outside the village is covered with cogon grass.
### 茅台(臺) → 茅 → 艹
- **definition:** plant
- **pinyin:** cǎo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts blades of grass
  - **interpretation:** 艹 is a pictogram representing grass or plants, resembling blades of grass. It is commonly used as a radical in other characters related to grass or vegetation.
- **examples:**
  - 他写(寫)字时(時)用艹作草字的偏旁。
    - Tā xiězì shí yòng cǎo zuò cǎozì de piānpáng.
    - He uses '艹' as the radical for grass in his characters.
  - 春天到来(來)时(時)，艹生长(長)得很快。
    - Chūntiān dàolái shí, cǎo shēngzhǎng de hěn kuài.
    - When spring arrives, grass grows rapidly.
### 茅台(臺) → 茅 → 矛
- **definition:** spear
- **pinyin:** máo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a bamboo spear with a ring in the middle ->
    - spear
  - **interpretation:** The character 矛(máo, 'spear') is a pictogram, directly illustrating the shape of a bamboo spear. The design reflects the basic components of the object it represents.
- **examples:**
  - 士兵举(舉)起矛。
    - Shìbīng jǔ qǐ máo.
    - The soldier raised his spear.
  - 古代战(戰)士用矛，冲(衝)锋(鋒)陷阵(陣)。

### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺)
- **traditional:** 臺
- **definition:** platform; stage
- **pinyin:** tái
- **components:**
  - 喬
    - qiáo
    - tall
  - 室
    - shì
    - building
  - 之
    - zhī
    - foot
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - abbreviated 喬 (qiáo, "tall") + 室 (shì, "building") with phonetic 之 (zhī) ->
    - 臺
  - **interpretation:** The character 臺 (tái, "platform") combines the idea of a 'tall' structure (depicted by an abbreviation of 喬 (qiáo, "tall")) with the concept of a 'building' (室 (shì)), representing the imagery of a tower or elevated structure. The phonetic element 之 (zhī) contributes the sound, reinforcing the pronunciation without altering the fundamental notion of elevation or a platform-like structure.
- **examples:**
  - 主持人站在台(臺)上。
    - Zhǔchí rén zhàn zài tái shàng.
    - The host stands on the platform.
  - 请(請)走到台(臺)前，接受奖(獎)项(項)。
    - Qǐng zǒu dào tái qián, jiēshòu jiǎngxiàng.
    - Please step to the front of the platform to receive the award.
  - 戏(戲)剧(劇)在大剧(劇)院的台(臺)上表演。
    - Xìjù zài dà jùyuàn de tái shàng biǎoyǎn.
    - The play was performed on the platform of the grand theater.
### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 喬
- **definition:** tall
- **pinyin:** qiáo
- **components:**
  - 高
    - gāo
    - high; tall
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** 高 (meaning 'high, tall') with a differentiating marker (variously a stroke, 屮, 止, 力, 九, or 夭) added
  - **interpretation:** The character 喬 (qiáo) is a differentiated form of 高 (gāo, 'high, tall'), created by marking it with additional strokes or components to distinguish it from the original character. This was done to differentiate its use for meanings specifically related to 'tall' or 'high', leading to its specific sense.
- **examples:**
  - 喬木常常长(長)得很高。
    - Qiáomù chángcháng zhǎng de hěn gāo.
    - Tall trees often grow very high.

    - Tā zhù zài yī zuò qiáo lóu zhōng.
    - He lives in a tall building.
  - 那座喬山看起来(來)壮(壯)观(觀)。
    - Nà zuò qiáo shān kànqǐlái zhuàngguān.
    - That tall mountain looks magnificent.

  - **description:** Depicts a tall building
  - **interpretation:** The character 高(gāo, "high; tall") visually represents a tall structure or building, symbolizing height or elevation. Unlike 京(jīng, "capital"), it is straightforwardly a representation of height.

  - **interpretation:** The character 室(shì, "room") combines the semantic element 宀(shì, "roof") with the phonetic 至(zhì, "arrive"), symbolizing a covered place where one stops or resides. This interpretation aligns with historical uses of 室 to denote a specific location or dwelling.

### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 室 → 宀
- **definition:** roof
- **pinyin:** mián
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a house with four walls ->
    - roof
  - **interpretation:** 宀(mián, "roof") is a pictogram representing a house with four walls. It emphasizes an enclosed space, distinguishing it from similar structures like 广(guǎng, "broad") which depicts a building with three walls. This makes 宀 a logical choice for representing a roof in various characters.
- **examples:**
  - 含有宀的汉(漢)字代表家的温(溫)暖。
    - Hán yǒu mián de hànzì dàibiǎo jiā de wēnnuǎn.
    - Chinese characters that include the radical '宀' represent the warmth of home.
  - 屋顶(頂)遮风(風)挡(擋)雨，家园(園)散发(發)温(溫)馨。
    - Wūdǐng zhē fēng dǎng yǔ, jiāyuán sànfā wēnxīn.
    - The roof shields from wind and rain, and the home radiates warmth.

### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhī
- **components:**
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 一
    - yī
    - one; the beginning place
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 止 ('foot') + 一 ('beginning place') ->
    - originally 㞢 ('to go') ->
    - simplified to a point
  - **interpretation:** The original compound 㞢 depicted a foot 止 (zhǐ, 'foot') stepping on a line 一 (yī, 'one; the beginning place'), indicating the concept of 'to go'. The footprint evolving into a point symbolized direction or movement, ultimately abstracted into 之 (zhī, 'of; possessive particle'), representing directionality or connection, as in 'of'.
- **examples:**
  - 天空之蓝(藍)让(讓)人心旷(曠)神怡。
    - Tiānkōng zhī lán ràng rén xīnkuàngshényí.
    - The blue of the sky makes people feel relaxed and happy.
  - 树(樹)之影在湖面上摇(搖)曳。
    - Shù zhī yǐng zài húmiàn shàng yáoyè.
    - The shadow of the tree sways on the surface of the lake.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 之](@media/glyph4e4b.png)
### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之 → 止
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 趾
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 龰
    - yù
    - stylized feet
  - 手
    - shǒu
    - hand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Original: Foot pointing up with 3 toes and a sole ->
    - Stylized as 龰 ->
    - Derivative 趾 refers to original 'foot' meaning
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicting a footprint with toes and a sole, 止 (zhǐ, "foot") represents the foot. The character's form resembles a foot with three toes, analogous to how the hand is represented with fingers in other characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)的止需要静(靜)养(養)。
    - Tā shòu shāng de zhǐ xū yào jìng yǎng.
    - His injured foot needs adequate rest.
  - 他走路时(時)小心谨(謹)慎，因为(爲)止若受伤(傷)便难(難)前行。
    - Tā zǒu lù shí xiǎo xīn jǐn shèn, yīn wèi zhǐ ruò shòu shāng biàn nán qián xíng.
    - He walks carefully because if his foot gets injured, it becomes difficult to move forward.

### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之 → 止 → 趾
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 足
    - zú
    - foot
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - halt
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 足 (zú, "foot") + phonetic 止 (zhǐ) ->
    - toe
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 足 (zú, "foot"), indicating the general area involved, with 止 (zhǐ) providing the sound and potentially suggesting the idea of a part of the foot that 'halts' or 'stops' progression, which naturally leads to the notion of a toe.
- **examples:**
  - 他的脚(腳)趾受伤(傷)了。
    - Tā de jiǎozhǐ shòushāng le.
    - His toe is injured.
  - 她用脚(腳)趾轻(輕)轻(輕)地踢了一下球。
    - Tā yòng jiǎozhǐ qīngqīng de tī le yīxià qiú.
    - She gently kicked the ball with her toe.
  - 在沙滩(灘)上散步时(時)，我感受到沙子在我的脚(腳)趾间(間)流动(動)。
    - Zài shātān shàng sànbù shí, wǒ gǎnshòu dào shāzi zài wǒ de jiǎozhǐ jiān liúdòng.
    - While walking on the beach, I felt the sand flowing between my toes.
### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之 → 止 → 趾 → 足
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a leg ->
    - originally depicted as ⽦ ->
    - represents 'foot'
  - **interpretation:** The character 足(zú, 'foot') is a pictographic representation of a human leg, which directly portrays the concept of a 'foot'. The pictographic origin emphasizes its fundamental meaning in the language.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)后(後)，他的足不能动(動)。
    - tā shòushāng hòu, tā de zú bù néng dòng。

  - 小明打球时(時)，不小心扭伤(傷)了足。

    - When Xiaoming was playing ball, he accidentally twisted his foot.
  - 我每天锻(鍛)炼(鍊)足部。
    - wǒ měitiān duànliàn zúbù。

### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之 → 止 → 龰
- **definition:** stylized feet
- **pinyin:** yù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a stylized footprint pointing upward ->
    - originally meaning 'foot' ->
    - later forms like 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') refer back to original meaning
  - **interpretation:** 龰 (yù, 'stylized feet') is a pictogram showing a footprint pointing up, originally indicating the concept of a foot. The character 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') evolved from this and retains the reference to the original meaning. It visually resembles a sole with three toes, similar to representations of the human hand in characters like 爪 (zhuǎ, 'claw'), 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), and 又 (yòu, 'again').
### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之 → 止 → 手
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a hand with fingers; top stroke is a bent over middle finger, horizontal strokes represent fingers
  - **interpretation:** The character 手 (shǒu, "hand") is a direct pictorial representation of a human hand with all five fingers, which distinguishes it from similar characters representing claws or simplified fingers. This visually conveys its meaning as a hand clearly.
- **examples:**
  - 他用手写(寫)字。
    - Tā yòng shǒu xiě zì.
    - He writes with his hand.
  - 妈(媽)妈(媽)牵(牽)着(著)我的手走路。
    - Māmā qiān zhe wǒ de shǒu zǒu lù.
    - Mom holds my hand while walking.
  - 他的手很温(溫)暖，带(帶)给(給)我力量。
    - Tā de shǒu hěn wēn nuǎn, dài gěi wǒ lìliàng.
    - His hand is very warm, giving me strength.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 手](@media/glyph624b.png)
### 茅台(臺) → 台(臺) → 之 → 一
- **definition:** one; the beginning place
- **pinyin:** yī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:** A horizontal stroke representing the concept of 'one'.
  - **interpretation:** The character 一(yī, "one") is a simple horizontal line signifying the singular and unified concept of 'one'. It directly represents being singular or the number one.
- **examples:**
  - 我有一个(個)苹(蘋)果。
    - Wǒ yǒu yī gè píngguǒ.
    - I have one apple.
  - 他只看到一只(隻)鸟(鳥)，飞(飛)进(進)了花园(園)。
    - Tā zhǐ kàn dào yī zhī niǎo, fēi jìn le huā yuán.
    - He only saw one bird, which flew into the garden.
  - 一条(條)直路通向远(遠)方。
    - Yī tiáo zhí lù tōng xiàng yuǎn fāng.
    - One straight road leads to the distance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 一](@media/glyph4e00.png)

## 茅台(臺)
### máo tái
